# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus TSDB Head Series Limit Exceeded

## Your Task

Prometheus crashes with 'out of bound samples' when cardinality is high. Find the Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that (1) enforce the head block series limit and (2) handle out-of-order or out-of-bound samples in the TSDB head.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

71-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented the Go source files in the Prometheus repository that handle head block series limits and out-of-order/out-of-bounds samples. 

## Summary

I found **4 key Go source files** in `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` that implement the required functionality:

1. **tsdb/head.go** - Enforces series cardinality limits via the `SeriesLifecycleCallback` interface and `getOrCreateWithOptionalID` method
2. **tsdb/head_append.go** - Validates sample ordering with `appendable`, `appendableHistogram`, and `appendableFloatHistogram` methods; handles OOO sample insertion with the `insert` method; processes samples at commit time with `commitFloats`, `commitHistograms`, and `commitFloatHistograms`
3. **tsdb/head_append_v2.go** - Performs fast-path out-of-bounds rejection when OOO support is disabled
4. **tsdb/ooo_head.go** - Implements the `OOOChunk` data structure that stores out-of-order samples in time-ascending order

The implementation uses a sophisticated 5-step pipeline:
- Fast-path OOB checks (V2 appender)
- Sample appendability validation (appendable methods)
- OOO chunk insertion (insert method)  
- Commit-time processing (commit methods)
- OOO chunk data structure management (OOOChunk)

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

Cardinality Limit Enforcement\\n\\nThe head block series limit is enforced through the **SeriesLifecycleCallback** interface (tsdb/head.go:234), which is called during series creation. The key method is **getOrCreateWithOptionalID** (tsdb/head.go:1844) which calls the PreCreation callback before creating a new series. If this callback returns an error (e.g., due to cardinality limits being exceeded), the series creation is rejected and the error is propagated up to the appender.\\n\\n## Out-of-Order and Out-of-Bounds Sample Handling\\n\\nThe TSDB head block handles out-of-order and out-of-bounds samples through a sophisticated pipeline:\\n\\n### 1. Fast-Path Out-of-Bounds Check (tsdb/head_append_v2.go:127-132)\\nWhen out-of-order support is disabled (oooTimeWindow == 0), samples with timestamps before minValidTime are immediately rejected with ErrOutOfBounds. Sample Insertion into OOO Chunks (tsdb/head_append.go:1799)\\nThe **insert** method handles out-of-order samples by inserting them into OOO chunks. When the OOO chunk reaches capacity (oooCapMax), a new OOO chunk is cut and the old one is memory-mapped. The actual insertion into the OOO chunk data structure is delegated to **OOOChunk.Insert** (tsdb/ooo_head.go:37).\\n\\n### 4. OOO Chunk Data Structure (tsdb/ooo_head.go)\\nThe **OOOChunk** maintains samples in time-ascending order using binary search-based insertion. Duplicate timestamps are rejected, and samples are stored uncompressed for efficient sorting during OOO chunk compaction.\\n\\n## Error Handling and Metrics\\n\\nErrors during sample appending are tracked through prometheus metrics:\\n- outOfBoundSamples: Fast-path rejections when OOO is disabled\\n- outOfOrderSamples: In-order check failures (OOO disabled)\\n- tooOldSamples: Out-of-order samples outside the OOO time window\\n- outOfOrderSamplesAppended: Successfully inserted OOO samples\\n\\nThese metrics allow operators to monitor sample ingestion quality and identify configuration issues with scrape intervals or time synchronization.\"\n}\n",

Sample Appendability Validation (tsdb/head_append.go)\\nThree methods validate whether samples can be appended:\\n- **appendable** (line 643): Validates float samples for order and time bounds\\n- **appendableHistogram** (line 688): Validates native histogram samples\\n- **appendableFloatHistogram** (line 730): Validates float histogram samples\\n\\nThese methods return:\\n- isOOO=false, err=nil: Sample is in-order and can be appended\\n- isOOO=true, err=nil: Sample is out-of-order but within the OOO time window\\n- isOOO=true, err=ErrTooOldSample: Sample is too old, outside OOO window (OOO enabled)\\n- isOOO=false, err=ErrOutOfBounds: Sample is out of bounds (OOO disabled, t < minValidTime)\\n- isOOO=false, err=ErrOutOfOrderSample: Sample is out-of-order (OOO disabled, t < headMaxt)\\n\\n### 3. Sample Insertion into OOO Chunks (tsdb/head_append.go:1799)\\nThe **insert** method handles out-of-order samples by inserting them into OOO chunks. When the OOO chunk reaches capacity (oooCapMax), a new OOO chunk is cut and the old one is memory-mapped. The actual insertion into the OOO chunk data structure is delegated to **OOOChunk.Insert** (tsdb/ooo_head.go:37).\\n\\n### 4. Commit-Time OOO Processing (tsdb/head_append.go:1310-1600)\\nThe **commitFloats**, **commitHistograms**, and **commitFloatHistograms** methods process appended samples during commit:\\n- In-order samples are appended directly via series.append()\\n- Out-of-order samples are inserted via series.insert()\\n- Samples that fail appendability checks are tracked and metrics are updated\\n- The **handleAppendableError** helper (line 1275) categorizes errors and updates rejection counters\\n\\n### 5. OOO Chunk Data Structure (tsdb/ooo_head.go)\\nThe **OOOChunk** maintains samples in time-ascending order using binary search-based insertion. Duplicate timestamps are rejected, and samples are stored uncompressed for efficient sorting during OOO chunk compaction.\\n\\n## Error Handling and Metrics\\n\\nErrors during sample appending are tracked through prometheus metrics:\\n- outOfBoundSamples: Fast-path rejections when OOO is disabled\\n- outOfOrderSamples: In-order check failures (OOO disabled)\\n- tooOldSamples: Out-of-order samples outside the OOO time window\\n- outOfOrderSamplesAppended: Successfully inserted OOO samples\\n\\nThese metrics allow operators to monitor sample ingestion quality and identify configuration issues with scrape intervals or time synchronization.\"\n}\n",
